3 BASELINE (SECTION B PART 1)
3.9 Soil
3.9.1 Introduction
This section presents the characterization of the Soil component, in accordance with what is established in the
Law No. 19,300 on General Bases of
l Environment and the Regulations of the Evaluation System
Environmental (D.S. No. 40/2012, modified by D.S. No. 30/2023, both of the MMA).
The Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate
(hereinafter the Project) corresponds to the set of parts, works and actions that will allow the
construction, operation and closure of a mining site and a clay processing plant, material
present in the area, which, due to natural effects, is highly weathered, with the presence of
rare earths in clay minerals. The Project will be developed mainly in the commune of Penco,
Province of Concepción, Biobío Region, without prejudice to the fact that part of the works are located in the commune
of Concepción, on the border with the Commune of Penco.
3.9.2 Objectives
3.9.2.1 General Objective
Characterize the soil natural resource of the area of influence of the Project, from its physical properties.
chemicals and their agricultural potential.
3.9.2.2 Specific Objectives
• Identify the general characteristics of the soil in the area of influence of the Project through
bibliography review, determining a condition of the site.
• Describe the morphological characteristics of the soil through field work.
• Collect soil samples to characterize the physical-chemical properties in the laboratory.
• Evaluate the risk of activation of erosive processes in the area of ​​influence of the Project.
• Determine the class of land use capacity based on the morphological description, analysis
of its physical-chemical properties and the context of the landscape in which it is inserted.
3-1
==================================================================================
PAGE 12
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B-Part 1)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
3.9.3 Area of Influence
The area of influence (AI) of the soil component is determined by the geographical space in which
which the parts, works and/or actions related to the Project will be located, and is directly
associated with the potential effects of the authorization of temporary and permanent works, such as loss,
compaction, erosion and/or deterioration of the physical, chemical and biological properties of the soil, such as
This is indicated in the “Guide for the description of the soil, flora and fauna components of terrestrial ecosystems in
the SEIA” of the SEA (2015). The magnitude of the impact due to loss and compaction corresponds to the
direct projection on the ground of works and activities, while erosion is associated
to certain conditions of materiality, climate and biological activity.
In this context, the area of influence (AI) of the soil component corresponds to an area of 235.69
hectares, which are determined by the location of the parts, works and actions
contemplated in the construction and operation of the Project (169.19 ha), plus a buffer of 20 m (66.5 ha)
considering the risks of activation of erosive processes due to the slopes that occur in the AI
(Figure 3-1), in relation to interior works and roads. Annex 3B-16 presents the AI of the
component in digital format.

3.9.4 Methodology
To carry out the characterization of the soils in the area of influence, the “Guideline for the Study of
Soils” SAG (2011, rectified 2016), in accordance with what is recommended in the “Evaluation Guide
Environmental: Soil natural resource” SAG (2019a).
The soil description allows providing the physical and chemical characteristics of the soil profile and
morphological
of the land to determine its Use Capacity Class (CCUS). These classes
They allow existing soils to be ordered, according to their relative adaptability, to certain crops or to predict their
productive potential, according to the critical or limiting attributes it presents. The criteria of the
mentioned SAG guideline, establishes categories of arable land from Class I to IV and non-arable,
from Class V to VIII, predicting an approximate productive potential in accordance with the
critical or limiting attributes that it presents. Table 3-1 summarizes the eight CCUS and the
associated productivity levels.
Table 3-1. Classes of usability and appropriate uses.
Increased intensity of use
Grazing Cultivation
CCUS
Wildlife and ecotourism Reforestation Very
Moderate Intensive Restricted Moderate Intensive
intensive
I Suitable for all uses. For cultivation it hardly requires conservation practices
II Suitable for all uses. For cultivation, simple conservation practices are required.
III Suitable for all uses, more intensive conservation practices in cultivation
IV Suitable for various uses, restrictions for some crops
V Suitable for grazing, reforestation or wildlife development
VI Suitable for extensive grazing, reforestation and wildlife
Suitable for reforestation and wildlife, in general
VII
unsuitable for grazing
Suitable for life preservation
wildlife or recreation, not suitable
VIII
for agricultural production,
grazing or forest material
Source: Ferreira, 2004
3.9.4.1 First stage of cabinet
In the first stage of the cabinet, the quantity and preliminary location of the pits was defined through the
compilation of bibliographic background, aiming at representativeness and detail
suitable within the area of influence.
3-4
==================================================================================
PAGE 15
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B-Part 1)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
The establishment of homogeneous soil units1 was carried out considering photointerpretation
geomorphological and other indicators (geoforms, hydrography, exposure, vegetation, uses, among others)
on the Google Earth® platform, as well as through the analysis of elevation models or
pending, all through geographic information systems. It is necessary to highlight that the units
homogeneous correspond to a recognizable, differentiable and representable element on a plane
thematic at a certain scale.
The work scale is defined in accordance with the objectives and level of detail required by the study in
based on “File SU-04: Soil” of the “Guide for the description of the area of influence: Description of the
soil, flora and fauna components of terrestrial ecosystems in the SEIA” (SEA, 2015), which allows defining
the necessary observation points on the homogeneous units for an adequate survey
of information. For this project a moderately high level has been used (1 observation
every 6.23 ha) (Table 3-2).
Table 3-2. Complementary sheet to define scales and number of observations in soil studies
Scale
Objective Level of Detail Number of Observations
Cartographic
Very high (Very intensive) 4 or more per ha 1:2,500
High (intensive) For normal lifting. 1 for every 0.8 to 4 ha 1:10,000
Moderately high (detailed) AI 1 soil description every 5 to 25 ha 1:25,000
Moderate (semi-detailed) 1 every 20 to 100 ha 1:50,000
Moderate (semi-detailed) For survey of 1 every 20 to 100 ha 1:50,000

3.9.4.2 Field survey
The data collection was carried out through the analysis of soil specialists in two campaigns.
of land: August 4 to 5 and November 6 to 10, 2023. The objective was to validate and complement the
information obtained in the office stage, through the use of those tools that
constitute a soil study: analysis of the landscape and its relief forms, identification of the state and
current use of the use, morphological description of representative pedons and soil sampling for,
subsequently, determine its physicochemical properties in the laboratory.
Yo. Physical and morphological characterization of the soil
The description of the soil is developed based on those characteristics or attributes that are required
to determine the CCUS of a given soil unit, considering the criteria provided in the
“Guideline for soil study” of the SAG 2011 (rectified), ordered descending below,
according to relative incidence on the classification:
Approximation criteria: these are those that allow soils to be classified according to whether or not they can be
tilled, grouping them into arable and non-arable soils, these are:
a) Depth class (cm)
b) Slope class (%)
c) Type of surface stoniness (% stones and % gravel)
d) Drainage class
Definition criteria: are those that, in combination with the grouping of approximation criteria,
allow you to determine
the CCUS. These are:
• Textural class
• Class of usable water (cm c.a.)
• Subsurface stoniness class (%)
• Erosion class
• Climate (frost and wind free period)
3-8
==================================================================================
PAGE 19
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B-Part 1)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Special criteria: are those that describe a particular existing condition, these are:
• Flood class
• Salinity class (dS m-1)
• Sodicity / alkalinity classes
The current erosion characterization was defined according to surface characteristics of the site, such as
grooves, cracks, erosion pedestals or pavements, presence of gullies, among others. The attribute of
Slope is determined with a clinometer on the ground.
The presence of carbonates was established in the field through the addition of drops of HCl (acid
hydrochloric) at 10% considering the methodology of the “Guide for Soil Description” FAO (2009).
Additionally, criteria were identified such as: color (Munsell Color 2009), redoximorphic traits,
structure, consistency, roots and porosity; was finally complemented with a photographic record of
each sampling point.
ii. Physical and chemical characterization of soil in the laboratory
For the determination of the parameters pH, salinity (electrical conductivity), organic matter,
sodicity (RAS), calcium carbonate, apparent density, texture and usable water (through
obtaining the permanent wilting point, field capacity and apparent density); was applied
following procedure: 1) sample extraction; 2) packaging and labeling; 3) provision in
containers and 4) transportation to the laboratory. The analyzes are carried out in the UC Agroanalysis Laboratory
accredited by the Agricultural and Livestock Service, according to current payrolls.
3.9.4.3 Third stage of cabinet
i. Identification of homogeneous units and CCUS
In this stage, the tabulation and organization of data collected in the field, the description and
analysis of results, both field and laboratory; and if necessary, the
cartography of homogeneous units, either by the reclassification of slopes, of topographic units
or the identification of intervened environments (roads or earthworks) that could not be
represented through photointerpretation of the initial cabinet stage. This data analysis
allowed:
• Validate and complement the information previously defined in the study stage of
secondary information.
• Define usability classes according to the interpreted characteristics.
• Conclude on the productive potential of the soil, whether agricultural, forestry or for grazing, or on
its potential use in environmental terms.
3-9
==================================================================================
PAGE 20
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B-Part 1)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
ii. Preparation of Slope Map
A slope map was made considering the ranges defined in the Soil Study Guideline.
(SAG, 2011), which has been prepared based on the topographic information collected by Digimapas Chile
for which the altimetry was obtained semi-automatically for a working scale of 1:2,000, with
equidistance between curves of 1 m and index curve every 5 m.
iii. Determination of usable water
The laboratory results and the physical and morphological characterization of the soil allowed us to determine the
usable water column, using the methodology of the guide “Soil physical analysis methods”
(Sandoval et al. 2011), using the following equation:
(𝐶𝐶−𝑃𝑀𝑃)
𝐻𝐴 = ∗𝐷𝑎∗𝑍∗(1−𝑃)
100
where,
HA = Water height (cm c.a.)
CC = Field capacity (%)
PMP = Permanent wilting point (%)
Da = Apparent density (g cm-3)
Z = Depth (cm)
P = relative fraction of stoniness
3.9.5 Results
3.9.5.1 Classification of Edaphic Zones of Chile
The Project is located in the edaphic area called “Arid Mediterranean Zones” (Luzio, 2010),
specifically in the area of soils
Hills of the Coastal Mountain Range. On these soils, the relief is
pronounced, with slopes that vary from 5% to 8% and from 8% to 15% in the hillside sectors; from 30 to
50% and more than 50% in the hill areas themselves. The parent material corresponds to rock
metamorphic, with different degrees of weathering, but with its recognizable schistose structure that
It still manifests itself in the lower horizons of the soils. From a geographical point of view –
physiographic, this sector constitutes an extension of the VII Maule region, so the division
administration of the country does not necessarily coincide in this case with the features of the landscape, as it does
could occur in other sectors of the country. Red and reddish brown colors continue in the 5YR shade, the
fine and very fine textural classes, generally with an increase in the fine fraction towards the horizons
lower. The depth of the soil is generally greater than one meter, the structures are made of blocks
3-10
==================================================================================
PAGE 21
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B-Part 1)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
strong medium subangular roots and the distribution of fine and medium roots is common to abundant in
contact with the underlying rock.
3.9.5.2 CIREN Agrological Study
According to the Agrological Study for the VIII Region (CIREN, 1999), the Project area is located on
the soil associations Constitución (KT) variation KT-5, and Treguaco (TG) with variations TG-3 and TG-
4. A smaller area (less than 1% of the project) is considered non-land, since it is identified
as an intervened area.
• Constitution Association (KT): It presents a deep, well-evolved, residual soil, formed by
made from metamorphic rocks, especially slates, well evolved, has a loamy texture
sandy clay on the surface and silty clay at depth. It is deposited on a
substrate made up of highly weathered metamorphic rocks with a clay matrix that allows the
deep root development. It is located in the highest altitude area of the Coastal Mountain Range, and
the western slope of the Coastal Mountain Range (Santis, 2005).
• Treguaco Association (TG): Deep soil, well evolved and formed from metamorphic rocks
especially micasites and highly weathered gneiss; silty clay loam texture throughout the profile and
of brown colors in shades 10YR and 7.5YR on the surface and dark brown in shade 7.5YR on
depth. It rests on a substrate made up of highly weathered metamorphic rocks with
high mica and quartz content. Within the Coastal Mountain Range, it preferably occupies the sectors
heights and the eastern slope in contact with the granite formation. They are well structured soils,
friable, with good porosity that allow good root development (CIREN, 1999). Within the
variations present in this Association, both TG-3 and TG-4 are found in the area of
Project location.
Both associations have an assigned CCUS of VII, mainly due to the limitations of
earrings. Figure 3-3 shows the distribution of the CCUS in the Project AI.

3.9.5.3 Agroclimatic District
The area of influence of the Project is located in the “Concepción” district according to the AGRIMED classification.
(2017), which is characterized by being a suprathermal warm temperate type with sub-humidity regime.
wet dry. The temperature varies
ranged between a January maximum of 23.6°C (max of 26°C and min of 20.5°C
within the district) and a July minimum of 7.4°C (max of 8.7°C and min of 6.6°C within the district).
It has an average of 345 consecutive frost-free days. In the year there is an average of 0
frost The period of temperatures favorable to vegetative activity lasts 12 months. Register
annually 1,502 degree days and 129 hours of cold accumulated until July 31. The average precipitation
annual is 374 mm and a dry period of 8 months, with a water deficit of 900 mm/year. The period
Wet lasts 3 months during which a water surplus of 69 mm is produced.
3.9.5.4 Current and Potential Erosion
The project is located in 2 communes, however, the largest area is in the commune of
Penco, commune on which the following erosion analysis is carried out.
CIREN (2010) points out that, for the Commune of Penco, 63.5% of the soils do not appear to be eroded, while
that 22% present some degree of erosion, mainly with signs of moderate erosion (See Table

3.9.5.5 Description of Homogeneous Units
The results of the physical and morphological description of the terrain, and the laboratory results are
presented in Annex 3B-15, where the description of the soil profiles, holes and points is attached.
of observation that allowed defining the UHS, and the analysis of the physical and chemical parameters was
present. With the information collected, a homogeneous soil unit and another
unit that is not classified as land because it is intervened, mainly roads and areas
industrial.
Hills: it is the most representative unit of the AI. It is characterized by developing in hilly sectors, with
pronounced slopes, with the characteristic of presenting a surface horizon of brighter colors
dark, due to the presence of organic matter. Clay levels on the surface are presented
lower when compared with the lower horizons, showing textures between clay loam and loam.
on surface.
The structure is usually of the granular type or subangular blocks, moderate to strong, and of medium to
thick. The presence of roots can be observed throughout the profile, essentially in the horizons
superficial, in sizes ranging from fine, very fine to medium. In general, no stoniness is observed
superficial and only in some cases is stoniness found in the profile. The limit between horizons
It is usually linear. No reaction to HCl was observed in any profile.

The acidity of the soil presents values between acid and alkaline, with a greater presence of acidic levels and

Regarding the electrical conductivity (EC), it is concluded that the soils of the area are not saline and the sodicity
is less than 5, therefore, corresponding to non-sodic soils. For all soil samples
present in Annex 3B-15, an EC < 2.dS/m and a RAS < 5 were obtained. On the other hand, the alkalinity,
based on the amount and expression of effervescence of the soil samples when applying HCL to the soil in
terrain, was presented for all
samples as non-alkaline.

3.9.6 Synthesis and Conclusions
The area of influence of the Project includes an area of 235.69 ha and is located in the
communes of Penco and Concepción, Province of Concepción, Biobío Region.
The soils are found in the Arid Mediterranean Zone, specifically in the Cerros soil area.
of the Coastal Mountain Range. The CIREN Agrological Study (1999) positions it on soil associations
Constitución (KT) (with the KT-5 variation) and Treguaco (TG) (TG-3 and TG-4 variations), both with CCUS
VII. A smaller area (less than 1%) is considered non-soil, since it is identified as an area
intervened. Regarding the agroclimatic classification, the district is “Concepción” according to the classification of
AGRIMED (2017), which has an average of 345 consecutive days free of frost and temperature varies
between a January maximum of 23.6 °C (max of 26 °C and min of 20.5 °C within the district) and a minimum of
July 7.4 °C.
He is
study on “Determination of current and potential soil erosion in Chile” (CIREN, 2010)
establishes that the categories of “severe” and “severe” potential erosion predominate in the Project area.
“moderate” representing 91.9% of the area of influence, which has as its main parameter
The relief is relevant, marked by steep slopes.
Two homogeneous soil units (UHS) called “Cerros” and “Quebrada” were identified. The first
represents 206.12 ha (87.5%) of the area of influence and is classified with CCUS VIs2 due to the slope limitation
equal to or greater than strongly wavy. It is defined as moderately to deep soils, well
drained to imperfect drainage, no surface stoniness to moderate stoniness. They have textures
fine and medium, presenting in some soil profiles described a clayey texture. For the
subsurface stoniness, different ranges are generally observed, the most common being to observe
soil profiles without stoniness to slight stoniness, to a lesser extent moderate stoniness.
As for usable humidity, in general they present regular to good usable humidity; it
above is associated with the fact that the soils in the area correspond to deep soils.
The homogeneous unit “Quebrada” represents 4.33 ha (1.8%) of the area of ​​influence; comprises 5 phases
which are classified by the pending limitation with CCUS IV, VI, VII and VIII, except the QBR-05 phase with CCUS
VIs8 which has usable water as a limitation. It is defined as thin to deep soils, drainage
poor to imperfect, and without surface stoniness. They have fine and medium textures (loamy to loamy
clayey). For subsurface stoniness, it is most common to observe soil profiles without stoniness.
As for usable humidity, in general they have regular usable humidity.
An “Intervened” area was also identified, covering 25.24 ha (10.7%) of the area of ​​influence. Due
to the intervention of the soil natural resource, the Capacity Class criteria do not correspond (N.C.).
Land Use. They are areas composed of roads and forestry facilities, mainly.

Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of

The SAG Guideline establishes that CCUS VI soils are non-arable soils and correspond to unsuitable soils.
for tillage when the restrictive parameter is the slope. Its normal use is livestock and forestry,
except when they have been classified in this category due to salinity conditions (> 4 dS/m), situation in
which its use is given by the adaptability of certain species to saline soils. Soil restrictions
They are more severe than in Class IV.
Regarding the occurrence of intense rain events, the records of days in which precipitation
exceeds a high threshold (95% percentile) show a decrease on an annual scale in the period
evaluated (1985-2019). However, there is agreement between the different projection models
climate about a potential increase in extreme precipitation events in the months of
summer, although no significant trend is observed for this type of events in other seasons
of the year.
Regarding other climatic trends that may determine the possible evolution of the soil component
In the face of climate change, it is recommended to review the precipitation and temperature trends described
for the hydrology, hydrogeology and water quality components. There are no antecedents in ARClim
on climate risks specifically applicable to the soil component.

3.10 Plants (flora and vascular vegetation)
3.10.1 Introduction
This section provides the characterization of the Plants component (flora and vascular vegetation),
in accordance with the provisions of Law No. 19,300 on General Bases of the Environment and its
modification through Law No. 21,600, which creates the Biodiversity and Protected Areas Service and the
National System of Protected Areas, and the Regulation of the Environmental Assessment System (RSEIA),
modified through Supreme Decrees (D.S.) No. 40/2012 of the Ministry of the Environment
(MMA) and the D.S. No. 30/2024 which approves modification to Supreme Decree No. 40, of 2012, of the
Ministry of the Environment, which establishes the Regulations for the Impact Assessment System
Environmental.
This characterization corresponds to the description of the current situation of the vegetation formations,
at the level of coverage and species present in them, and the flora of the area of influence (AI) of the Project.
This report was prepared based on available bibliographical background and the results of
flora and vegetation obtained from the campaigns carried out between 2022 and 2023. These campaigns
correspond to the autumn 2022 season, carried out between May 30 and June 4, the winter campaign
2022, held between August 22 and 27; the spring 2022 campaign, from November 21 to 25; the
2023 summer campaign, executed between January 9 and 13 and January 23, the winter campaign
2023, carried out between July 10 and 11, and finally the spring 2023 campaign, carried out in two
field campaigns, the first between September 25 and 29 and the second between December 18 and 22;
the details and efforts of which are presented later in this document.
The area of influence has a surface area of 673.62 ha and corresponds to the vegetation formations that
will be affected by the Project works (whether permanent or temporary), taking as a limit
of these the physiographic characteristics of the terrain, such as slopes, ravine bottoms, summits,
plains or changes in slope and/or exposure, also consider formations that will not be seen
intervened by the Project works in order to have a continuum for the study.
3.10.2 Objectives
3.10.2.1 General Objective
The objective of this report is to characterize the state of the vegetation and flora present in the area.
of influence of the Project. For this, the following specific objectives have been set:

terrestrial ecosystems in the SEIA (SEA, 2015), Methodological guide for the consideration of change

• Identify areas that are sensitive to vegetation or flora within the area.
of influence.
3.10.3 Determination and justification of the area of influence
The Area of Influence (AI) corresponds to the spatial extent in which the impacts are manifested.
direct environmental aspects of the Project under evaluation, and where the spatial limits of the
vegetation and flora receptors that must be characterized in the baseline, so that the evaluation
of impacts is exhaustive and complete. In this way, the area of influence has been established “with the
purpose of defining whether the project or activity generates or presents any of the effects, characteristics or
circumstances of Article 11 of Law No. 19,300, or to justify the nonexistence of said effects,
characteristics or circumstances”, as indicated in article 2, letter a) of the D.S. No. 40/2012.
Considering what the Guide for the description of the area of influence of the SEA (SEA, 2015) indicates for
define this area for the Project, two specific criteria are considered:
• Surface where the Project works will be located and where vegetation loss will be generated due to
the materialization of the works (cutting or intervention area). This area considers the entire
the Project works, whether temporary or permanent works.
• Surface of residual vegetation that, due to the construction of the Project, could be seen
fragmented and could lose its ecosystem functions, being reduced to patches or “islands.”
within the Project area.
In this way, for the Plants component (Vascular Flora and Vegetation) the area of
influence (AI) as the surface that will be directly affected by the materialization of the works (whether

EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
temporary or permanent works), because their construction has the effect of removing
total or partial vegetation and, consequently, the loss of flora present in the place. It is also
include sectors where works that directly intervene in this component are not presented,
corresponding to the vegetation formations surrounding the area of the future Project, whose extension is
established in accordance with the natural limits of the vegetation formations given by the
physiographic characteristics of the terrain, such as slopes, ravine bottoms, summits, plains,
changes in slope and exposure; as well as by artificial limits such as roads, canals, areas
industrial, among others. The objective of incorporating this surrounding or additional surface is
characterize the existing vegetation for the analysis of impact or lack of effects as indicated in the
definition of the area of influence.
In this way, the surface of the AI is 673.62 hectares and is located in the communes of Penco and

3.10.4 Methodology
3.10.4.1 Bibliographic background of the area of influence
In order to establish the biogeographic framework in which the project will be located, they are used as
reference the works of Gajardo (1994) “Natural Vegetation of Chile” and, by Luebert and Pliscoff (2019),
“Bioclimatic and vegetation synopsis of Chile.”
Yo. The Natural Vegetation of Chile (Gajardo, 1994)
This study was developed based on biogeographic criteria and terrain background, establishing
four levels of aggregation; ecological region, ecological sub-region, plant formation and type community.
The first three have cartographic representation and therefore defined distribution areas. The
The fourth level disaggregates plant formations based on micro-environmental criteria, level
of alteration due to natural catastrophic processes and/or due to the effects of anthropogenic influence. This level does not
It has cartographic representation. For each of these communities the system provides a list of
the most representative species.
ii. Bioclimatic and vegetation synopsis of Chile (Luebert and Pliscoff, 2019)
This was developed based on bioclimatic criteria (thermotypes and ombrotypes that define floors
bioclimatic) and vegetational (plant formations). The basic unit of analysis is constituted by
the concept of vegetation floor, defined as “spaces characterized by a set of
zonal plant communities with uniform structure and physiognomy, located under conditions
homogeneous mesoclimatic, which occupy a certain position along a gradient of
elevation, at a specific spatio-temporal scale.” The vegetation floors have representation
cartographic, and in general they account for the potential vegetation at a greater level of detail than the
Gajardo classification (1994).
iii. Projects with Environmental Qualification Resolution
Projects with a current Environmental Qualification Resolution (RCA) were identified, whether they were
Environmental Impact Declarations (DIA) or Environmental Impact Studies (EIA), located in the territory
close to the area where the works and actions of the Project will be located. For this, information was collected
of all projects entered into SEIA2 using the project search service by Region,
In addition, there was access to downloadable information, on the same website, in Excel and KMZ format. The
Search criteria used were:
2 https://www.sea.gob.cl/

• Geographic location: Projects from the Biobío Region that had works or
activities within the limits of the Communes of Concepción and Penco. Specifically, it

2023.

3.10.4.2 Photointerpretation of Satellite Images
The characterization of the vegetation or current land use was carried out based on the interpretation of a
mosaic of freely accessible satellite images (Google Earth, Bing and ESRI) and a LiDAR image of the year
2022 (Annex 3B-25) that contains the area of influence of the Project, which is segmented according to
to patterns that the vegetation presents such as texture, color and grain, allowing to differentiate areas and
homogeneous cartographic units. As a result, digital coverage is preliminarily obtained
of polygons classified according to vegetation formations, which may correspond to:
• Forests
• Thickets
• Grasslands
• Grasslands
• Plantations
• Areas without vegetation (Summits, rocky outcrops, river bed)
• Other uses (Agricultural, industrial, urban)
3.10.4.3 Collection of information in the field to characterize flower
to and
vegetation
To describe the vegetation and record the flora present, field campaigns are carried out in
which the area of influence is toured on foot, identifying and characterizing the polygons
photointerpreted in the office, quantitatively through forest inventory plots and/or
qualitatively through observation points. Qualitative variables are understood as the identification
of plant formations, while the quantitative variables correspond to the number of individuals
by species (trees, shrubs and succulents) and their coverage present in each vegetation unit. The
Data recording is carried out on a portable electronic device (Tablet) with the Nviro Flora application
(https://nviro.cl/).
Sampling points are assigned through stratified random sampling, which is designed in
cabinet, and consists of assigning one or more points, according to the surface, to each registered polygon

previous.
Sampling validation is obtained from the calculation of the sampling error. To do this, you have to,
each plot estimates a density value that is close to the true density value of the stand. Of this
Thus, the estimate is subject to an error that depends both on the variability of the density parameter,
as well as the number of sampling units used to estimate. Any sampling estimate is
affects a sampling error, which is based on the distribution of the estimator, in this case the density
(Nha).

3.10.4.4 Characterization of Vegetation and Flora
The characterization of the vegetation is carried out by collecting information at the sampling points.
established in cabinet, occupying forest inventory plots of 500 or 1,000 m2 depending on the
vegetation formation. In case of not being able to carry out a forest inventory plot, a point is made
observation.

Rare Earth Concentrate
For the characterization of the flora, floristic inventories are carried out, which are done in the same
sampling points assigned in the cabinet, recording the relative abundance of the composition
floristics using an adaptation of the Braun-Blanquet (1964) methodology.
The aforementioned methodologies are documented in the Guide for the description of the
soil, flora and fauna components of terrestrial ecosystems in the SEIA, of the Evaluation Service
Environmental (2015).
Each of the methodologies of the mentioned types of sampling are explained below.
Yo. Sample Type
Vegetation eo
To define the size of plots, the upper size limit indicated by Mueller is considered.
Dombois and Ellemberg (1974), which indicates that the inventory plots should be between 200 – 500 m2.
For the specific case of native forests, the surface is 1,000 m2 as mentioned in the Guide
for the description of the soil, flora and fauna components of terrestrial ecosystems in the SEIA (SEA,
2015).
a) Sampling in forest inventory plots with a surface area of 500m2
This type of sampling is carried out in scrub formations, where all
the tree and shrub individuals present within the plot, measuring the crown coverage in
two directions and their respective height, in order to obtain quantitative data related to the level of
both vertical and horizontal stratum, which allows relating the participation of the different species
registered within the plant community. Additionally, the arboreal individuals'
diameter at chest height (DBH).
b) Sampling in forest inventory plots with a surface area of 1,000 m2
This type of sampling is carried out in forest formations and plantations, where they were identified and
quantified all the tree and shrub individuals present within the plot, measuring the
diameter of cups in two directions and their respective height, in order to obtain quantitative data
related to the level of both vertical and horizontal stratum, and numerical values that allow
relate the participation of the different species recorded within the plant community.
Additionally, the diameter at breast height (DBH) was measured for arboreal individuals.
c) Observation Points
This methodology is used in those sectors where it is not possible to carry out a forest inventory, either
due to accessibility issues or because there are no tree and/or shrub individuals to count (for example
(for example, grasslands and meadows). In these sectors, the vegetation is described through variables
qualitative. The variables included in this description are the presence of species and structure of
the formation, identifying the dominant and accompanying species by stratum.

ii. Type of Flora Sampling
a) Braun-Blanquet method based on sampling plots
At each sampling point, floristic inventories were carried out, in which the scale of
abundance-dominance of each species according to a value scale (Table 3-15). This method
corresponds to a combination of the coverage data obtained in the forest plots, plus a
visual estimation of cover/abundance for herbaceous species.
Table 3-15. Braun-Blanquet abundance-dominance scale
Population Attributes Registry
7 Any number of individuals, with coverage greater than 90% of the plot
6 Any number of individuals, with coverage between 75 and 90% of the plot
5 Any number of individuals, with coverage between 50 and 75% of the plot
4 Any number of individuals, with coverage between 25 and 50% of the plot
3 Any number of individuals, with coverage between 10 and 25% of the plot
2 Any number of individuals, with coverage between 5 and 10% of the plot
1 Any number of individuals, but with less than 5% coverage
+ Few individuals, with reduced coverage (<1%)
r Solitary individuals, with very low coverage (<1%)
Source: Modified from Braun Blanquet, cited in Mueller-Dombois and Ellemnerg (1974)
In the case of detecting a species that is not found within a plot, it is included
the same way in the floristic list, in order to associate it with the vegetation formation that is wanted.
describe and to which it belongs. In this case, the code “p” is applied, so that the species is
recorded, even if it has not been sampled on the plot.

Microrouting consists of georeferencing tree individuals classified as threatened3 (In
Critically Endangered, Endangered, Vulnerable) according to the conservation status determined in accordance with the
official sources cited in the MMA priority minutes (Memorandum DJ No. 387/2008) present in
the area of influence. Specifically, the species Pitavia punctata and Gomortega keule are considered,
both classified as Endangered (D.S. No. 151/2007), and Citronella mucronata classified as Vulnerable (D.S.
No. 16/2016).
In the office, through cartographic analysis, the priority search areas and the layout are determined.
of the route to follow on the ground, in order to systematize the search process in the area of influence.
To georeference the individuals of interest, high-precision geodetic equipment (Satlab Sl 700) is used.
and to characterize each individual, the following data is recorded per individual:
• scientific name,
• common name,
• diameter at chest height (DBH) (cm),
• diameter at neck height (DAC) (cm),
• total height (m),
• phytosanitary status (good, bad, fair, dead),
• conservation status (according to Species Classification Regulations (RCE)),
• stems per vine (scions that sprout from stumps).
For the definition of phytosanitary status, the “good” category considers all or almost all of the
green foliage without symptoms of water and/or nutritional deficiencies or damage from biotic agents, “fair”

The classifications of current use of grassland, scrubland, wetlands and forests correspond to formations
vegetables themselves. For its part, Law No. 20,283/2008 (Law for the recovery of native forests and
forest development), regulations and associated decrees, regulates said plant formations by naming them
according to specific characteristics, and breaks them down. In this way, the classification of the
Plant formations are defined as follows:

• Grassland: Corresponds to a plant formation where species of the herbaceous biological type dominate.
both annuals and perennials, and the coverage of trees and shrubs is less than 5%.
• Shrubland: They correspond to vegetation structures in which habit species predominate.
shrubby, and may present tree elements in its composition, but with a percentage of
canopy coverage of less than 10%, and that additionally do not correspond to xerophytic formations.
According to Law No. 20,283, scrublands can form Xerophytic Formations, which
are defined as “plant formation, made up of native species, preferably
shrubs or succulents, from areas of arid or semi-arid conditions located between Regions I and
VI, including the Metropolitan and XV and in the interior depressions of Regions VII and VIII.”
The same legal body defines native or autochthonous species, as “original tree or shrub species”.
of the country, which has been officially recognized as such by supreme decree." In D.S. No.
68/2009 of MINAGRI, which the law refers to, establishes, approves and makes official the list of
tree and shrub species native to the country.
Considering the above, the bushes are described by separating those that
make up a Xerophytic Formation and those that do not make it up.
• Forest: According to article 2 of Law No. 20,283/2008, forest is that site populated with
plant formations in which trees predominate and that occupy an area of at least
5,000 square meters, with a minimum width of 40 meters, with tree canopy coverage that
exceeds 10% of said total area in arid and semi-arid conditions and 25% in circumstances
more favorable (coverage considered for the present study). Within the concept of forest,
They have the following distinctions:
• Native forest: In accordance with article 2
of Law No. 20,283/2008, corresponds to that
forest formed by native species, coming from natural generation, regeneration
natural, or plantation under canopy with the same species existing in the distribution area
original, which may have accidental presence of exotic species distributed randomly.
• Native forest preservation: In accordance with the provisions of Law No. 20,283/2008 and its
modifications presented in Law No. 21,600/20234, the Native Preservation Forest is that,

permanent or temporary, stagnant or flowing, sweet, brackish or salty, including extensions of

Ramsar applies a broad definition of wetlands, covering all lakes and rivers, swamps and
marshes, wet grasslands, peat bogs, estuaries, and other coastal areas, and man-made sites such as
dams, reservoirs and others.”

considered as a wetland, at least one of these three attributes proposed by
Cowardin et al., (1979), considered in the current legislation for the delimitation of urban wetlands,
but also applicable to any type of wetland:
• At least periodically, the land supports predominantly hydrophilic vegetation.
• The substrate is predominantly hydric soil (poorly drained or undrained) or;

3.10.4.6 Vegetation coverage map adjustment
Once the field campaigns were completed, the information was validated; likewise, it
proceeded to include elements that were not possible to deduce directly from
satellite information. The information incorporation process was carried out by adjusting the
homogeneous vegetation units (polygons) and their attribution with additional information such as:
species, coverage, density, among others.
The final result corresponds to the vegetation cover map, where through the data
quantitative data recorded in the field, the vegetation is classified, first defining whether they are
regulated by Law No. 20,283/2008, to later define the dominant species of the formation. This
Dominance corresponds to the species with the greatest coverage according to the data obtained from the
forest inventory plots, as follows:
• Native forest of “species
• “Species Y” scrub,
• Planting of “species Z”, among others.
In addition to the characterization of the vegetation formations, it is included in the description
vegetation cover ranges5, obtained through the forest inventory plots, following the
following categorization:
• Very scarce (coverage between 0 – 1%)
• Very open (coverage between 1 - 25%),
• Open (coverage between 25 - 50%)
• Dense (coverage between 50 - 75%) and
• Very dense (coverage between 75 - 100%).

In the case of unique susceptibility to the effects of Climate Change, the maps are consulted
climate risks available in the Climate Risk Atlas (ARCLIM-MMA)7 for the component
flora and vegetation.
Among the best known responses to the effects of climate change on biodiversity, are
find the effect on the geographical distribution of species and ecosystems. Through ARCLIM it is possible
access climate change risk maps for these two levels of biodiversity organization
(species and ecosystems) for continental Chile. Current species distribution data are generated
based on data on species occurrences, obtained from the Global Biodiversity Information Facility
(GBIF) and Botanical Information and Ecological Network (BIEN). To date, the data incorporated allows
access maps of 440 species of flora. On the other hand, distribution data at the ecosystem level are
generated from the classification of the vegetation levels of Chile, presented in the proposal of
bioclimatic and vegetation synopsis of Chile (Luebert and Pliscoff, 2019), defining 125 units for Chile
continental.
The climate information was extracted from the regional climate model that allows obtaining a set of
climatic variables for two time periods; current period (1980-2010) and future period (2035-
2065). The spatial resolution for continental Chile of the climate variables is 5 km.
To define climate risk at the species level, ARCLIM uses the final database of occurrences,
extracting the current and future values of the climatic parameters of average temperature and
annual precipitation by species. This methodology is based on the concept of safety margins in
7 https://arclim.mma.gob.cl/
3-48
==================================================================================
PAGE 59
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
the response of flora and fauna species with records of occurrence in continental Chile, to variations
in climate change based on the characterization of its current tolerance.
To define risk at the ecosystem level, ARCLIM uses the results of the species-first approach
that allows establishing a climate tolerance metric for the species, calculated for each unit
analysis (5 km pixel). With this data, calculate the average risk value per ecosystem and commune,
for both flora and fauna species.
The risk to climate change on the loss of flora is defined by the following formula.
Risk = Threat x Exposure x Vulnerability
The threat corresponds to the difference between the current and future climate (defined for temperature
annual average and annual precipitation). Exposure is defined by the loss of surface area with
natural vegetation in each terrestrial ecosystem, defined by the conservation category in the red list
of Chilean ecosystems, this criterion defines percentages of loss for the definition of each category,
where Vulnerable implies a 30% loss, Endangered 50% and Critically Endangered 80% (Pliscoff, 2015).
The vulnerability is obtained from the quotient between the sensitivity (safety margin for temperature
and precipitation, added for flora) and the adaptive capacity of the species. At ARCLIM, the capacity
adaptive is defined by the distribution range of a species (niche breadth), species
s with a
small distribution range, will indicate a low niche breadth and will be more sensitive to changes
futures in climate variables. The risk represents the deviation of current climatic margins
regarding the future that the set of flora and fauna species in a 5 km pixel could support.
Finally, ARCLIM groups the risk values into quantiles to obtain five levels (very low, low,
medium, high, very high) to climate change for flora and fauna, by ecosystems and communes on a national scale.
For its part, the risk to climate change on the vigor or greenness of native forests is defined by the
following formula.
Risk = Threat x Exposure x Sensitivity
The threat corresponds to the variation in the joint incidence of droughts and heat waves between the climate
historical and future on the continuity of photosynthetic productivity. The exhibition is defined as
index that represents the communal area covered by native forests, where 0 corresponds to the
absence of native forests and 1 to the highest proportion. In ARCLIM the general approach for the
Exposure estimation includes the combination of four databases: map of coverage of the
soil of Chile (Zhao et al., 2016), the global database of forest cover change (Hansen et al.,
2013), the results of the project “Catastro of the native vegetation resources of Chile: Monitoring of
changes and updates” (CONAF 2011) and the Bioclimatic and Vegetational Synopsis database
published by Luebert and Pliscoff (2006) to distinguish some vegetation floors of interest. The
3-49
==================================================================================
PAGE 60
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Sensitivity represents the potential effect of soil water content, elevation and soil index.
topographic humidity in the greenery of the forest under the context of changes in precipitation and
temperature. ARCLIM uses two main metrics to quantify native forest sensitivity
as response variables to changes in temperature and precipitation: the proportional change in the
NDVI (Cp) and the trend of NDVI over time. The risk represents increased loss of greenery
of the native forest between the historical period and the future. Finally, ARCLIM groups risk values
in quantiles to obtain five levels (very low, low, medium, high, very high) to climate change for the
increase in greenery loss by commune.
The risk to climate change on native forest fires and forest plantations is defined by
the same formula indicated above, but with different definitions of the variables.
Risk = Threat x Exposure x Sensitivity
The threat represents the variation in the incidence of temperatures above 30°C (conducive to
occurrence of forest fires) between the historical and future climate, which was determined by the relationship
between heat waves and forest fires recorded between 1985 and 2018 (195,358 fires). The
exposure is defined as the communal area covered by native forest and forest plantations,
where 0 represents absence of forests and plantations and 1 corresponds to the highest proportion. At ARCLIM
The general approach for estimating exposure includes the combination of four bases
data: land cover map of Chile (Zhao et al., 2016), the global land change database
forest cover (Hansen et al., 2013), the results of the project “Catastro of natural resources
native vegetation of Chile: Monitoring of changes and updates” (CONAF 2011) and the database
of the Bioclimatic and Vegetational Synopsis published by Luebert and Pliscoff (2006) to distinguish some
vegetation floors of interest. Sensitivity represents the probability of a fire occurring.
give the environmental conditions of each commune in terms of human activity, topography and
soil covers. ARCLIM determines the probability using the Machine Learning (ML) model, the
which groups the variables that represent different characteristics of the territory. The risk represents the
variation in the probability of occurrence of forest fires
s as a result of heat waves, between
the historical and future period. Finally, ARCLIM groups the risk values into quantiles to obtain
five levels (very low, low, medium, high, very high) to climate change for increased occurrence
of forest fires by commune.
On the other hand, to define the climate risk of those species that are not available in the
ARCLIM platform, its distribution models were developed through the Maxent tool
of the R software.
Species distribution models show a probability of presence of the species in each
pixel (5x5 km2 cells), with 0 being the minimum value (no probability) and 1 being the maximum value
probability. The Maxent tool estimates this probability of presence from a set of
3-50
==================================================================================
PAGE 61
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
explanatory variables under historical climatic conditions (1980-2010). In this case, the modeling
carried out using as explanatory variables the average annual evapotranspiration, precipitation
annual cumulative, annual average daily solar insolation, annual average minimum temperature
daily and annual average of the daily maximum temperature. Once verified that the model reproduces
adequately the distribution of the species under historical climatic conditions, the
probability of occurrence of the species under future climate conditions (2035-2065) under the scenario
RCP 8.5 (scenario of intense greenhouse gas emissions).
For the interpretation of species distribution models, it is necessary to keep in mind that these
They do not represent the current or future density of the species, but rather represent the probability that in
a certain pixel there are climatic conditions conducive to the existence of a species. In this
In this sense, the models can give a probability of the presence of a species greater than zero in
sectors where there are no records of its occurrence, to the extent that the climatic conditions
are similar to sectors where the species is present.
3.10.5 Results
3.10.5.1 Bibliographic background of the area of influence
In order to establish the biogeographic framework in which the Project will be located, they were used as
reference the works of Gajardo (1994) “Natural vegetation of Chile” and Luebert and Pliscoff (2019)
“Bioclimatic and vegetation synopsis of Chile.”
Yo. The Natural Vegetation of Chile (Gajardo, 1994)
According to Gajardo (1994), the Project area is inserted in the Deciduous Forest Region, in the Sub-Region
of the Llano Deciduous Forest, specifically in the formation of the Concepción Deciduous Forest
(Figure 3-12).
3-51
==================================================================================
PAGE 62
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Figure 3-12. Vegetation formations, according to Gajardo (1994)
Source: GAC
The Deciduous Forest Region extends from 33° to 41° south latitude in a low-lying territory
temperate climate with brief summer drought. In its northern distribution it occupies mountainous positions on the
80-100 m altitude to go progressively towards the south occupying the intermediate depression. The
essential characteristic that distinguishes this Region is the presence of tree strata of the species of the
genus Nothofagus that have large deciduous leaves.
The Llano Deciduous Forest Sub-Region represents deciduous forests, which are
distributed in low situations, beyond 36° south latitude, occupying the central depression and the
low-altitude mountainous reliefs; In certain sectors it approaches the ocean coast. It is a territory
rich in vegetation possibilities, generally finding a strong penetration of species
laurifolias in the typical physiognomy of dominant deciduous trees. It is the geographical area of the oak
(Nothofagus obliqua).
As noted above, the area of
Project creep is specifically located in the
formation of the Concepción Deciduous Forest, which extends along the lower and middle slopes of the
Coastal Mountain Range, in the Biobío Region, presenting a humid phase towards the oceanic slope and

but it has been almost completely replaced by Pinus radiata and/or Eucalyptus plantations.

ii. Bioclimatic and Vegetational Synopsis of Chile (Luebert and Pliscoff 2019)
According to Luebert and Pliscoff (2019), the Project is located in two formations. One corresponds to the Forest
Sclerophyllous, specifically the vegetation floor Mediterranean coastal sclerophyllous forest of Lithrea
caustica - Azara integrifolia, and the other called Deciduous Forest formation, specifically at
vegetation floor Mediterranean coastal deciduous forest of Nothofagus obliqua - Gomortega keule
(Figure 3-13).
3-53
==================================================================================
PAGE 64
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Figure 3-13. Vegetative floors, according to Luebert and Pliscoff (2019)
Source: GAC
The Sclerophyllous Forest is the largest formation in the Mediterranean area of central Chile, where
Numerous studies have been carried out that make it a relatively well-known vegetation.
and there are several general reviews. It is found in the lower parts of the coast and the low interior
semiarid to humid conditions. The dominant species are hard-leaved trees. coastal areas,
more humid, are strongly influenced by the presence of lauri-sclerophyllous elements such as
Cryptocarya alba and Peumus boldus, while in the drier inland areas they tend to be more
dominant Quillaja saponaria, Lithrea caustica and Kageneckia oblonga. The altitudinal limit of the vegetation
arborea is marked by communities dominated by Kageneckia angustifolia.
The vegetation floor Mediterranean coastal sclerophyllous forest of Lithrea caustica - Azara integrifolia
corresponds to a floor of sclerophyllous forest vegetation in which the tree stratum is dominated by
Lithrea caustica, Cryptocarya alba and Azara integrifolia, showing a more oceanic character than the flat
above (Andean Mediterranean sclerophyllous forest of Quillaja saponaria - Lithrea caustica), with presence
of elements of the maulino deciduous forest. It is very diversified, being important the
presence of the woody Lomatia hirsuta, Rosa rubiginosa, Sophora macrocarpa and Myrceugenia obtusa and
3-54
==================================================================================
PAGE 65
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section B)
Terrestrial ecosystems
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
of the epiphytes Bomarea salsilla, Lardizabala biternata and Proustia pyrifolia as characteristic elements
os
local.
Regarding its dynamics, the repeated cutting and burning of vegetation (anthropogenic pressures) produce a
very severe degradation, but grazing pressure in these coastal areas is considerably
minor. The vegetation has been greatly degraded, giving way to a largely arborescent scrub.
of its extension, but in some cases it reaches a forest physiognomy with considerable development
structural, both horizontal and vertical. The presence of large extensions in adjacent areas that
have been replaced by Pinus radiata plantations causing the invasion of introduced species
such as Teline monspessulana and Rosa rubiginosa. This vegetation floor in turn constitutes the bushes
secondary substitution of the deciduous forest of Nothofagus glauca and Persea lingue. It is located in
low western slopes of the Coastal mountain range of the Libertador Bernardo O'Higgins regions,
Maule and northern Biobío, between 0-600 m, under the influence of bioclimatic floors
mesomediterranean subhumid and humid lower hyperoceanic and oceanic.
For its part, the Deciduous Forest is a dominant formation in the low and mountainous areas of the
Mediterranean-temperate transition of Chile and in the Andes mountain range throughout the central-southern zone of
Chile, where the seasonality of the climate determines that the dominant species lose their leaves in
winter. All these species belong to the genus Nothofagus, where species can be distinguished
deciduous with large leaves (N. alessandrii, N. alpina, N glauca, N. obliqua) and small leaves (N. antarctica,
N. pumilio). The former are dominant in the lowest and warmest areas, while the latter
They are in the coldest and frequently high parts, defining the altitudinal limit of the tree vegetation.
The only exception is Nothofagus macrocarpa, the northernmost species of the genus, which
Being a large-leaved species, it tends to occupy elevated positions and define the limit of the vegetation.
arboreal in the coastal mountain range of central Chile. Communities dominated by others
Large-leaved Nothofagus contact the sclerophyllous forests to the north, and have many
elements of these forests, while the southernmost areas border with laurel forests and
evergreens, whose influence is also observed in its floristic composition.
The vegetation floor Mediterranean coastal deciduous forest of Nothofagus obliqua - Gomortega keule
presents a deciduous forest vegetation dominated by Nothofagus obliqua, with the presence of elements
laurifolios, highlighting the differential presence of Gomortega keule, Podocarpus saligna, Gevuina avellana,
Lomatia dentata, Caldcluvia paniculata, Lapageria rosea and Aextoxicon punctatum, despite being found
currently restricted to only a few specific enclaves.
Regarding its dynamics, a significant proportion of surface that has been fragmented and replaced
by Pinus radiata plantations and the scarcity of studies make it very difficult to make considerations about
the dynamics of this floor. Some ancient antecedents indicate that human intervention has generated
the replacement of forests by shrublands and floristically highly diversified secondary grasslands that,
In some cases they preserve part of their original composition, with a strong component of elements

3.10.5.2 Characterization of vegetation and flora
i. Sampling Points
Six land campaigns were carried out within the area of influence of the Project between the years 2022 and
2023. The first in the autumn season, between May 30 and June 4, 2022, the second was carried out in
winter, between August 22 and 27, 2022; the third in the spring 2022 season, during the
November 21 to 25; the fourth in summer, between January 9 and 13, 2023 and January 23, 2023
same year; the fifth in the winter season, executed between July 10 and 11, 2023; and the last in
spring between September 25 and 29 and between December 18 and 22, 2023. In all
Professionals from the flora and vegetation area participated in the campaigns.

iii. Natural Environment
They correspond to those sectors where the vegetation presents characteristics of composition and
structure close to natural conditions and where the effect of anthropogenic activity has not generated
notable changes in the physiognomy of the formations.
In the area of influence of the Project, the presence of 121.02 ha (18%) of natural environments was recorded,
made up of forest, grassland and scrub land uses, with an area of 41.84 ha, 11.79 ha,
67.39 ha respectively (Table 3-32).
Considering what is stated in the D.S. No. 259/1980 of MINAGRI (Technical Regulation Decree Law No.
701/1974), within the area of influence, two Forest Types are identified that, according to the definition of the
Article 19 of the aforementioned Regulation, correspond to:
• Sclerophyllum: is one that is represented by the presence of at least one of the
species indicated below, or by the association of several of them. The species that
constitute this type are: Quillay (Quillaja saponaria), Litre (Lithrea caustica), Peumo (Cryptocarya
alba), Hawthorn (Acacia caven), Maitén (Maytenus boaria), Carob (Prosopis chilensis) Belloto
(Beilschmiedia miersii), Boldo (Peumus boldus), Bollén (Kageneckia oblonga), Molle (Schinus
latifolius) and other species with a geographical distribution similar to those already indicated.
• Oak-Raulí-Coigüe (Nothofagus obliqua-Nothofagus alpina-Nothofagus dombeyi): is one that is
is represented by the presence of any of the three species or a combination of
them, constituting the association or any of them more than 50% of the individuals per hectare
with a diameter of not less than 10 cm. at 1.30 meters high.

introduced herbaceous plants such as Alisma lanceolatum, Bromus hordeaceus, Galega officinalis, Polygonum
aviculare and Rumex acetosella and by the native grass Juncus procerus, together representing a
open vegetation cover (25-50%) (Figure 3-36). This unit presents a humid grassland physiognomy
because it is located in sectors with temporary flooding.
Within its floristic composition, there are also some shrubs such as Baccharis sagittalis,
Buddleja globosa, Muehlenbeckia hastulata and Teline monspessulana, and some isolated specimens of
Acacia melanoxylon, Acacia dealbata and Aristotelia chilensis, whose tree cover did not exceed 1%,
with an average height of 1.5 meters.
They were not recorded within the formation of species in the conservation category.

and some specimens of the exotic trees Pinus radiata and Eucalyptus globulus, with a cover

3.10.5.5 Vascular Flora in the Area of Influence
A total of 247 species of vascular plants were recorded in the area of influence. The floristic catalog
of the AI is presented in Annex 3B-19 along with its taxonomic classification, phytogeographic origin, habit
of growth and belonging to the D.S. No. 68/2009 of MINAGRI.
In Table 3-51 it can be seen that of the total number of species recorded in the area of influence, 93.5%
corresponds to the Division Magnoliophyta (231 species), within which the Class Magnoliopsida
It groups the majority of the taxa with 78.5% (194 species) and the remaining 15% correspond to the Class
Liliopsida (37 species). Then the Pteridophyta Division continues with 14 species (5.7%), distributed
mostly in Class Polypodiopsida (13 species). Finally, for the Pinophyta Division,
recorded two species (0.8%) classified within the Pinopsida Class. The entire flora identified
in the area of influence of the Project represents 4.6% of Chile's flora, according to the catalog of
Rodríguez and Marticorena (2019).

iv. Specific Wealth by vegetation formation
Table 3-57 shows the specific richness by growth habit of the vegetation formations.
identified in the area of influence of the Project, being the Eucalyptus globulus plantation and the forest
feral Pinus radiata the units with the greatest richness, with 163 (66%) and 124 species (50.2%)
respectively, of a total of 247 taxa. Both formations correspond to intervened environments,
specifically to plantation and wild forest sub-use respectively.
Of the 163 species recorded in the Eucalyptus globulus plantation, 23 are arboreal in habit, within
of which the dominant species is found, however, the formation presents an important group of
native and endemic trees (19 species). In addition, 47 mostly native shrubs are recorded and
endemic and several herbaceous species (93 species) with mainly introduced origin.

Regarding the wild forest of Pinus radiata, the 124 species identified are distributed in 25

presents 36 shrub species, of which 14 are of endemic origin and 18 of native origin, and 63
herbs, which unlike the Eucalyptus globulus plantation, are mainly native.
Another formation that presents an important floristic richness is the wild Eucalyptus forest.
globulus with 92 species (37.2%). Of this total, 18 are trees distributed among endemic origins
(six species), native (eight species) and introduced (four species), 29 species are shrubs
mostly endemic and 45 correspond to herbs, distributed equally among the types
of endemic, native and introduced origins.
Then the natural vegetation formations continue, Teline monspessulana scrub, forest
native preservation of Nothofagus obliqua and native forest of preservation of Aextoxicon punctatum,
with a richness of 89 (36%), 80 (32.4%) and 79 (32%) species respectively. In the case of the bush
of Teline monspessulana presents a majority of native and endemic trees (12 species), however,
Four introduced species were also recorded within this formation. Next to the trees they identified
27 shrubs and 46 herbs of mainly introduced origin.
In the case of the native preservation forest of Nothofagus obliqua, with 80 species within its matrix
floristics, presents 25 trees, 23 shrubs and 32 herbs, which mostly correspond to species
native and endemic. For its part, the native preservation forest Aextoxicon punctatum, the 79 species
They are distributed among 26 trees, 26 shrubs and 27 herbs (annual and perennial), of which the majority is
native origin, followed by endemic species and thirdly those introduced to the country.

viii. Presence of native forest inside SNASPE units
According to the background reviewed and analyzed in this baseline of flora and vegetation, there is no
presence of this singularity in the area of influence of the Project.
ix. Activity in or adjacent to priority sites for national conservation
According to the Ordinary Office D.E. (SEA) N° 100143/2010 priority sites for conservation in the SEIA
correspond to 64, of which five are located in the Biobío Region (Isla Mocha marine area, Cerro
Cayumanque, Fundo Nonguén, Nevados de Chillán and Quebrada Caramávida). Of this group, the area of
Project influence does not overlap, or is not within the boundaries of some type of priority site
for national conservation.

According to the information and cartographic material available, there is no record that the area of
influence of the project is in or adjacent to protection areas in accordance with Law No. 18,378,
corresponding to those called “soil, forest and water conservation districts”, as well as
as well as areas with a ban on cutting trees in strips of up to 100 meters from public roads,
banks of rivers and lakes, and streams not susceptible to use, when required by the
conservation of tourist wealth.
xiv. Activity in or adjacent to or upstream of Wetlands
The area of influence of the Project does not overlap, or is not within the limits of any type of
Wetland listed in the National Wetland Inventory, of the Ministry of the Environment (2015),
whose last update is from 2020.

in the Penco commune, where the Project's area of influence is located.

Due to the above, the plant component may be affected by future changes in the
precipitation and temperature patterns. In accordance with what is indicated in Annex 1-11, the observations
of the historical period (1985-2019) show a significant trend of decrease in
precipitation on an annual scale at meteorological stations (Dichato, Carriel Sur and Cancha Los stations
Liters). Regarding future projections of rainfall, these remain with trends
negative, although not all models present statistical significance for this result. The
Historical records also show a significant increase in days without rain in the months of
autumn in the analyzed stations, a trend that is also observed for projections under a
climate change scenario.
Regarding changes in temperature, the information available in Annex 1-11 shows
an increase in a set of maximum temperature indicators, with greater significance in summer
and on an annual scale. Increases in heat waves are projected, and longer days and nights are generally expected
warm weather and progressive increases in temperature, especially in summer. This is expected to impact
an increase in the evapotranspiration demand of crops and increase the risk of fires
forestry. More background information available in Annex 1-11.
Regarding the potential effect of changes in climate on the vigor or greenness of native forests to
communal level, a very low value is estimated for the risk index of loss of greenness of the native forest.
Vigor or greenness represents the abundance of chlorophyll in the leaves, which is an approximation of the
photosynthetic capacity and growth potential of plants. Its decrease may represent a
decrease in growth, defoliation and death of parts of the crown or individuals (Table 3-65).

In the case of susceptibility to climate change at the species level, in ARCLIM it was possible to obtain
distribution models for three species of interest to the Project, for a historical period (1980-2010)
and future (2035-2065) in a scenario of intense greenhouse gas emissions,
corresponding to Citronella mucronata (Vulnerable), Gomortega keule (Endangered) and Pitavia punctata (In
danger). In addition, through the Maxent tool, distribution models were obtained for three other
species of interest: Asplenium trilobum (Vulnerable), Vestia foetida (Endangered) and Gardoquia multiflora
(Almost Threatened).
The projection of the probability of species presence is carried out using five climatic variables:
average annual evapotranspiration, annual accumulated precipitation, average annual solar insolation
daily, annual average of the daily minimum temperature and annual average of the maximum temperature
daily. The results available in Table 3-66 were calculated using the weighted average by
surface of the pixels coinciding with the area of influence of the Project. When interpreting the results,
It is necessary to keep in mind that the values represent the probability of presence of each species in
the area of influence in a historical period (1980-2010) and in the future period (2035-2065).

xvii. Presence of plant species protected by special regulations
In accordance with the floristic lists of the area of influence and according to environmental and sector regulations.
In force, three species regulated by special protection measures were recorded in the area of influence.
These correspond to Gomortega keule (queule) and Pitavia punctata (pitao), which are declared
natural monuments by the D.S. No. 13/1995 of MINAGRI which prohibits its cutting; and the species Lapageria
rosea (copihue) which presents a special regulation prohibiting marketing according to what
Decree No. 129/1971 (Modified by D.S. No. 121 of 1984) is stipulated, in addition to being declared a flower
national according to Decree No. 62 of 1977 of the Ministry of the Interior. As mentioned above, the
Construction of the Project will not involve individuals from Gomortega keule or Pitavia punctata.

3.10.6 Synthesis and conclusions
Regarding the background information collected in the six terren campaigns
or executed between the years 2022
and 2023, it was possible to quantitatively and qualitatively characterize the current situation of the formations
vegetation and flora existing in the area of influence of the Project (673.62 hectares). In total
They executed 515 sampling points distributed throughout the AI. In addition, 43 points of
additional sampling, carried out by the company Gesforam, between the months of August and December 2023.
It was determined that the intervened environments cover the largest surface of the area of influence, reaching
71% of the total area (478.37 ha), followed by the natural environment with 121.02 ha (18%) and in third
place the modified environment with 74.23 ha (11%). In general, it can be indicated that AI is composed
mainly by forest plantations and wild forests, followed by scrublands and
forest formations.
Regarding the vegetation formations corresponding to the intervened environment, those that present
The largest area within the area of influence corresponds to the plantation of Eucalyptus globulus, the
